---
title: "Applications vs Main Menu and Panels issues in Trusty"
date: 2014-08-12
forum: Installation &amp; Upgrades
---

### Post by cscj01 on 2014-08-12
I just upgraded from Precise 12.04.5 to Trusty 14.04.1 and I am using Gnome Flashback (I think that's the correct name for it now).  Except for two problems, things have worked okay to date.

First, in Precise, if I wanted programs to show in a different menu under the Main Menu, all I needed to do was drag the program icon from the right side to the menu on the left.  This does not work for me after upgrading.  Also, I cannot assign an icon to any new menus I create.  Finally, if I add new menus using Main Menu, they do not appear when I access Applications on my panel.  In fact, I am not sure if there is a correlation between what I see through the Applications menu from the panel and what I see when I open Applications>System Tools>Preferences>Main Menu.  The menus were changed from what I had in Precise, so I am trying to get them back to the way they were.

Secondly, when I boot, my panels do not appear.  I must execute gnome-panels to get them to show up.  Unfortunately, when I was struggling to get my panels visible, all my shortcut launchers disappeared.  Is it possible to get the panels I had before rather than the default ones?  When I first got my panels to appear, they were just as they were in Precise.

---

I can not do anything with Main Menu now and it is not using my .desktop files.  All I can do is add new menus, but the folder never appears when I go to the menus under Applications.  I can add new items using Main Menu, but those items never appear when using Applications.  Many of the applications I have installed never appear in the menus, and I have to enter the command from a terminal to launch them.  Most items are in a menu called Other, and there is no real organization to the menu structure.  Since I can't change anything using Main Menu, I do not know how to change them.  This is a real nuisance.

As for the panels, I have to manually start them after a reboot or a logon, which is another pain.  Surely there must be something I can do to straighten out this mess.

### Post by cscj01 on 2014-08-13
I added gnome-panel to the Startup Applications, and that seems to have fixed my panels issue.  However, I do have another issue related to panels.  For some reason, when I launch an application, I get 2 instances showing on my runnung applications panel: one on the left and one on the right.  Any ideas on this?

Another thing that is occuring is that my mouse scroll wheel is going in the opposite direction from how it was in Precise and all previous of Ubuntu.  It scrolls down when it used to scroll up and vice versa.  Once again, any help will be most appreciated.
Sorry, this is only in Firefox.  I'll check out mozilla forum for this.

---

### Post by cscj01 on 2014-08-13
Fixed the scrolling issue using Ubuntu Tweak>Tweaks>Miscellaneous>Natural Scrolling set to Off.

---

A few things come to mind but it's all only speculation at this point. For instance what is now flashback relies on 'unity-settings-daemon' and 'unity-control-center' now so maybe if the meta-package 'ubuntu-desktop' was not installed some configuration may have failed????

Or maybe the transitional package 'gnome-session-fallback' needs to be installed????

Or maybe the path to 'alacarte' is still looking in the wrong place - that had to be changed to not interfere with the menus in the new GNOME Classic session.

You'll notice [here]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=2220264") that I included Challenges and Known Issues. I still haven't figured that all out and it looks like we have yet another new challenge :icon_frown:

### Post by kansasnoob on 2014-08-17
I'm still focused on why gnome-panel fails to launch properly, and remember I've not been able to reproduce that, so I've been scanning those logs (which are huge in comparison to mine) and see a lot of errors in the apt.log that begin with *"Depends on pkg_name+version"* and end with *"can't be satisfied!"* Nothing jumps out at me as 'gnome-panel' specific but the fact that I can't reproduce the behavior + a multitude of errors in the upgrade logs indicate a somewhat borked release upgrade.

Of course you need only scan through the past few days of forum threads here to see how problematic the upgrade process can be. That said I think we should try a few very basic commands to try and determine if we can fix things or if a fresh install is in order. I have a dumb question first though - I see several things in the logs mentioning virtualbox and I've almost never used a VM (just a bit with testdrive) so I need you to tell me if this is installed on bare metal or if it's a VM. I suspect that you've just used that OS as a host for other VM's but I'm not smart enough to be certain.

Anyway it'd make sense to just try:

```
sudo dpkg --configure -a
```

```
sudo apt-get update
```

```
sudo apt-get dist-upgrade
```

```
sudo apt-get -f install
```

Of course any one of those, particularly apt-get -f install, may indicate the need for further action and you may need to repeat them in different orders if missing dependencies are indicated.

Some of the other menu issues you mention are actually design flaws, or entirely by design, such as the elimination of Sundry & Utilities. Not sure what this meant, "the .desktop files in `/.local/share/applications are not being used". Does that have to do with creating desktop launchers?

As far as the ~/.local/share/applications .desktop files not being used, here is my explanation for that statement.

I have all my previously configured menus from many Ubuntu versions in there, not in /usr/share/applications, because that is where alacarte puts user configured .desktop files.  Those menu structures (menus and applications or files) did not show up with the alacarte Main Menu application that is in Trusty.  The structure that showed up was /usr/share/applications .desktop files.  However, when I installed the Utopic version of alacarte, Main Menu showed the old structures I had created in the past along with the /usr/share/application .desktop files.  That is all well and good, but the Applications menu still only shows a portion of what is in ~/.local/share/applications along what is in /usr/share/applications.  By that I am totally confused unless some .desktop files in /usr/share/applications are overiding some of those in ~/.local/share/applications.  I presume this could be true if they have the same name in each directory.  I will check that out.

I hope that last explanation makes sense.

### Post by kansasnoob on 2014-08-22
Reinstallation varies greatly depending on your current drive and partition setup. Dual booters and those with multiple drives and/or partitions need to be acutely aware of this bug:

[https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/ubiquity/+bug/1265192](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/ubiquity/+bug/1265192)

So lets start with some very basic info. Please post the output of:

```
sudo parted -l
```

And:

```
df -H
```

And:

```
cat /etc/fstab
```

We'll likely need more info but that's a good place to start.

---

Given the overall complexity I'm seriously considering a dual boot of your existing Ubuntu (which we'd leave largely untouched) and a fresh install of Ubuntu right next to it on the same drive so it can be tweaked into 100% tip-top shape without disturbing anything that already exists. That way you can do it at your own pace and boot back into the existing install to get work done until the fresh install is 100% up to speed. If that sounds like a plan you'd be willing to pursue I wonder if it would be possible to reduce the % used to 40% or less (30% would be better)?

### Post by kansasnoob on 2014-08-23
I just had silly thought regarding troubleshooting the panel/menu problems. It's probably just silly and pointless but it won't take long and should be perfectly safe.

First go to System Settings > User Accounts and set auto-login to off just to play things safe. Then reboot just to be sure things are OK regarding the ability to boot, select the desired session, etc.

Next logout, select Guest, be sure to select a Flashback w/ Metacity session and see how the panels and menus act. If it's better than your user session there are some things we can try ............... might as well see if the Guest session is effected also ;)

---

### Post by kansasnoob on 2014-08-24
**Read this all before beginning, best to measure 2 or 3 times and then cut only once!!!!**

We need to work on two things, (1) adding / and swap to /etc/fstab, and (2) renaming some of the hidden dots in Home. Before we start just keep in mind that I'm only human so if things blow up you get to keep all of the pieces. Actually you should be fine if you're comfortable working in the terminal - like if the edits to fstab bork the ability to boot you may need to boot into recovery mode, enable networking to provide read/write privileges, then use the root shell + nano to comment out our edits. Clear so far?

Are you comfortable using nano? I seldom have to use it so I always have to ponder how to properly save and exit, but for the most part the instructions are at the bottom of the window, navigation is mostly done with the arrow keys. If you're not comfortable please take time to ask more questions before you begin!

In regards to (1) I need you to first check the output of:

```
cat  /etc/initramfs-tools/conf.d/resume
```

Make sure the UUID there matches this (without the quotes):

> /dev/sdc3: UUID="5b3c361f-14a1-45fa-bd52-49cfae3f331b" TYPE="swap" 

**[COLOR="#FF0000"]If it does not match STOP![/COLOR]**

Second check and make sure this is your current /etc/fstab:

```
# /etc/fstab: static file system information.
#
# <file system> <mount point>   <type>  <options>       <dump>  <pass>

proc	/proc	proc	nodev,noexec,nosuid	0	0
#Entry for /dev/sdd1 :
UUID=00AE2EA54F4183A2	/media/Data	ntfs-3g	defaults,nosuid,nodev,locale=en_US.UTF-8	0	0
#Entry for /dev/sdb1 :
UUID=3573b59f-77c9-460d-9a29-9f6730954125 /media/Data_One	ext4	errors=remount-ro	0
#Entry for /dev/sda1 :
UUID=9ef58828-ffae-4248-ad25-44596e6440d1 /media/Data_ext4	ext4	errors=remount-ro	0
#Entry for Samba Share drive g on cp2
#//cp2/g	/mnt/cp2	smbfs	iocharset=utf8,uid=1000	0	0

#Entry for NFS Server on drive g on cp2
cp2.local:/media/Ubuntu_Data_Backup/Data /nfs/Ubuntu_Data_Backup nfs _netdev,vers=3 0 0

#Entry for NFS Server shared documents on cp2
cp2.local:/media/cp2_data/ /nfs/cp2_shared_docs nfs _netdev,vers=3 0 0
```

I just want you to double check in case the output you pasted was somehow truncated in the copy-n-paste process. If that's correct we know we need to add entries for / and swap. So you'd have to run:

```
gksudo gedit /etc/fstab
```

And then add the edits highlighted in red, then save and quit:

```
# <file system> <mount point>   <type>  <options>       <dump>  <pass>
proc	/proc	proc	nodev,noexec,nosuid	0	0
[B][COLOR="#FF0000"]# / is on /dev/sdc1
UUID=b61632e9-7186-4ec9-9e4c-214c01d39a4e /               ext4    errors=remount-ro 0       1
# swap is on /dev/sdc3 
UUID=5b3c361f-14a1-45fa-bd52-49cfae3f331b none            swap    sw              0       0[/COLOR][/B]
#Entry for /dev/sdd1 :
UUID=00AE2EA54F4183A2	/media/Data	ntfs-3g	defaults,nosuid,nodev,locale=en_US.UTF-8	0	0
#Entry for /dev/sdb1 :
UUID=3573b59f-77c9-460d-9a29-9f6730954125 /media/Data_One	ext4	errors=remount-ro	0
#Entry for /dev/sda1 :
UUID=9ef58828-ffae-4248-ad25-44596e6440d1 /media/Data_ext4	ext4	errors=remount-ro	0
#Entry for Samba Share drive g on cp2
#//cp2/g	/mnt/cp2	smbfs	iocharset=utf8,uid=1000	0	0

#Entry for NFS Server on drive g on cp2
cp2.local:/media/Ubuntu_Data_Backup/Data /nfs/Ubuntu_Data_Backup nfs _netdev,vers=3 0 0

#Entry for NFS Server shared documents on cp2
cp2.local:/media/cp2_data/ /nfs/cp2_shared_docs nfs _netdev,vers=3 0 0

```
Now we need to finish enabling swap so run:

```
sudo update-initramfs -u
```

Be patient! It may take a minute or two to run! Wait until the command prompt shows up again!

Then we might as well reboot and hope for the best before moving on to (2).

If that worked OK then (2) should be a piece of cake. We just need to rename these hidden dots while booted into Ubuntu, but first remove 'gnome-panel' from the startup apps because we want to try things as they should be out-of-box:

```
.compiz                                   
.compiz-1                                 
.config      
.gconf                                    
.gconfd    
.gnome2                                   
.gnome2_private 
.local  
.profile
```
 
And then we'll need to rename one more hidden dot while at the login screen before logging in because it seems to be static in nature, that is it continues to change as your session is running:

```
.cache
```

Clear as mud?

So while booted into your user session run each of these (do not sudo, it's not needed and may mess up your read/write privileges):

```
mv .compiz .compiz_OLD
```
                                  
```
mv .compiz-1 .compiz-1_OLD
``` 
                               
```
mv .config .config_OLD
```    
  
```
mv .gconf .gconf_OLD
```
                                   
```
mv .gconfd .gconfd_OLD
```
    
```
mv .gnome2 .gnome2_OLD
```    
                               
```
mv .gnome2_private .gnome2_private_OLD
```

```
mv .local .local_OLD
``` 

```
mv .profile .profile_OLD
```

Then set auto-login to off and on reboot access the terminal from the login screen using Ctrl+Alt+F1 then run:

```
mv .cache .cache_OLD
```

And then "sudo reboot" and hope for the best.

If that improves things you'll either need to make all of your panel and menu tweaks individually or try restoring bits and pieces of those OLD hidden dots to see what works and what breaks things.

### Post by kansasnoob on 2014-08-24
> **cscj01 said:**
> Okay, I was able to reboot and log in with panels.  And some of my menus are correct.  However, there are items that were in my menus before I changed the names of the folders that are no longer there.  I suppose I can recreate most of them.  The problem seems to be that when I try to add a new menu with Main Menu, it will show in Main Menu, but not in Applications menu.  Additionally, I still cannot move items from one menu to another.  Finally, I cannot add a new item to an existing menu.  So while this has fixed my panels issue, my menu issues are worrse.

I assume the menu issue is then due to poor design :(

I know what we largely agreed on was to revert to what was the Quantal design because the Precise design no longer worked at all with the parts of GNOME version 3.10 that shipped with Trusty. It is not as slick as Precise was by a long shot and I've still not found a way to consistently backup an entire profile so each fresh install requires individual tweaking. A lot of the change was needed in order to not break GNOME's new Classic shell session.

There has been a lot of in-fighting between the lead maintainer of GNOME Panel and the other devs - one in particular - and one of the previous maintainers who is still heavily involved in Edubuntu has already suggested killing GNOME Panel in favor of adopting Mate in Edubuntu 16.04 .................. so who knows what the future will bring :confused:

But, let me make this perfectly clear, the current version of 'gnome-panel' (aka; the flashback session) will be supported in Trusty until April 2019, just as the Classic (no effects) session in Precise is supported until April 2017. I know I'm keeping about 30 of the 50+ puters I maintain on Precise, using the [archived 12.04.1 images]("http://old-releases.ubuntu.com/releases/12.04.1/") for reinstallations in order to avoid [HWE EOL]("https://wiki.ubuntu.com/1204_HWE_EOL") and the [Trusty HWE that shipped in 12.04.5]("https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Kernel/LTSEnablementStack#Kernel.2BAC8-Support.LTS_Kernel_Support_Schedule").

---

> Lo and Behold.  I can now add new menus and new items.  In order for a menu to display on the Applications menu, there must be at least one item on that menu.  Unfortunately, I still cannot drag and drop menu items from one menu to another.  So I must add the item and duplicate what is in the menu item I am trying to move.  That is a long and laborious process, but at least it is attainable.

One issue remains though.  I seem to be able to use only certain files (mostly .svg files and some .ico files) for my item and menu icons.  If I try to use a .png icon, it does not show next to the item after the save.  When I navigate to it from the Applications menu, I get the Ubuntu icon [ATTACH=CONFIG]255828[/ATTACH]with a black background and the diagonal slanted the other way.  Sorry, I couldn't find the one Ubuntu uses.

Edit:  Actually, it is not the type of file.  There are just some cases where the icon for the menu item shows correctly when selected, but when the item is saved, there is no icon.  And what shows on the Applications menu is as explained above.
